During initialization, these flags start as 0. But once a timeout occurs and they're set to 1, they're never reset during resume. This causes problems because:\n\n1. When the device resumes, azx_init_chip checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)` before initializing the command I/O, so the CORB/RIRB never get set up again. The flags need to be cleared either at the start of azx_init_chip or during the resume sequence to allow proper reinitialization. first_init, azx_init_pci is called after CORB/RIRB initialization. This ordering difference means that during resume, when azx_init_chip runs and checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)`, the flag still has its old value, causing CORB/RIRB setup to be skipped entirely.\n\nThe core problem is that hardware state flags like single_cmd persist across the reset without being cleared. When the hardware is reset via azx_reset, the corresponding software flags should also be reset to reflect the fresh state. The appropriate place for this would be within azx_reset itself or immediately after it's called in azx_init_chip, ensuring that mode-tracking flags are synchronized with the newly reset hardware.\n\nThe actual failure pattern is revealing: immediately after resume, codec communication fails, triggering a cascade of fallback attempts—switching to polling mode, disabling MSI, then single_cmd mode. After the first timeout sets single_cmd to 1, subsequent resumes don't reinitialize the CORB/RIRB because that flag prevents it.
